  374. This does not come with instructions, but once you get the hang of it, it does do a ballerina bun nicely. You have to tie your hair into a pony tail, pull hair through the sponge clip hole, close shut, pull down to the end of your pony tail and curl. My advice is to start the curl facing up and curl towards the top of your head so that way, when you fold the edges of the sponge clip in, the edges are facing down and you can let gravity help covering it with your hair. You then push your hair around those exposed edges and if you want, you can add a few bobby pins if you feel like it doesn't cover it all the way. Another tip for a more &#34;tight fit&#34;, after rolling your hair, I folded one side of the sponge clip and slid my hair over that part and then folding the other side of the sponge clip and pushing the hair over on that side, though it would look more like a spiral pattern than just a round bun. I do have to say that after wearing it all day and taking it off in the evening - got a bonus &#34;hair style&#34; of curly/wavy hair.

  448. my hair type:<br />dark brown, thick, unprocessed (natural), wavy<br /><br />likes:<br />takes 2 minutes to create a neat looking bun with the least amount of effort<br /><br />dislikes:<br />i took one star off because the inside wire is not thick/heavyweight enough to REALLY secure my very full head of hair on its own<br /><br />tips/comments:<br />-practice makes perfect, give it a week<br />-if you have little to no layers you will LOVE this. if you have many layers (i do) i find that i have to start winding the product at about halfway through the length of my hair, otherwise it starts to fall out way too much<br />-secure with a few pins if your hair is on the heavier side and/or heavily layered<br /><br />this works great for the price especially.<br /><br />i tie my hair in a pony and then put the hair through the center of the bun maker. then i close the opening and run it forward (in front of my face, not back towards my butt, lol) to the tips of my hair (actually,only to where my layers begin because if i put it through to the ends my layers begin to fall out). once i've rolled it as tightly or loosely as i want (different effect with each) and have reached my pony i spread out the hair a bit to cover the rest of the foam and then bend the foam wire around my pony. then i just play with the positioning making sure to cover the foam. voila! neat and tidy in a matter of minutes-no joke!<br /><br />tip: like i said my hair is pretty heavy so i sometimes use a second hair tie around the bun after it's been made, just to secure it in place. i've noticed if i don't use the second tie it can get loose and undone hours later.

  700. REVIEW<br />I really like these bun makers and I plan to order more. They are better made than I expected. The wire inside is sturdy enough to hold my hair all day and night (my hair is about 8 inches below my shoulders, layered and semi-fine textured). I want to order more because they are inexpensive enough and I would like to have back ups just in case. I would recommend these to anyone because they are so simple to use! They don't come with instructions but I will explain how to use them below for anyone interested.<br /><br />HELPFUL TIPS<br />I find these work best on hair that was washed the day before. Freshly washed hair is a bit too soft.<br />1. Put hair into a ponytail.<br />2. Spread the bun maker and place your pony tail through it.<br />3. Squeeze the bun maker closed around your pony tail to make a tighter fit.<br />4. Pull the bun maker to roughly 3/4 the length of your pony tail (I go about halfway because of my layers).<br />5. Roll your hair down until it touches your head and bend the bun maker into a circle.<br />6. Spread your hair evenly over the bun maker until it is completely covered.<br />I find it helpful to secure the hair closed around the bun maker with a bobby pin or a clear elastic to hold it in place.<br /><br />That's it! The whole thing takes about a minute. Less with practice. There are lots of youtube videos too that helped me. Just search &#34;sponge or foam bun maker&#34; and lots of things come up. I hope this helps!
